colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2020)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a><sup id="cite_ref-DEC2019JFK_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DEC2019JFK-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> FAA<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>John F. Kennedy International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>JFK</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KJFK</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>JFK</b>) (colloquially referred to as <b>JFK Airport</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, and one of the primary airports serving New York City. The airport is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic#2018_statistics" title="List of busiest airports by international passenger traffic">busiest international air passenger gateway</a> into <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USDT1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDT1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">20th-busiest airport in the world</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_United_States" title="List of the busiest airports in the United States">sixth-busiest airport in the United States</a>, and the busiest airport in the <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_the_New_York_metropolitan_area" title="Aviation in the New York metropolitan area">New York airport system</a>, having handled over 62.5 million passengers in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> More than ninety airlines operate from the airport, with nonstop or direct flights to destinations in all six inhabited continents.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FI_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FI-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>JFK is located in the <a href="/wiki/Jamaica,_Queens" title="Jamaica, Queens">Jamaica</a> neighborhood of Queens,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> 16 miles (26&#160;km) southeast of Midtown Manhattan. The airport features six passenger terminals and four runways. JFK is a hub for both <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, and it is the primary operating base for <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>. JFK was also formerly a hub for <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan Am</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">TWA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(1934%E2%80%931980)" title="National Airlines (1934\xe2\x80\x931980)">National</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tower_Air" title="Tower Air">Tower Air</a>.\n</p><p>The facility opened in 1948 as <b>New York International Airport</b><sup id="cite_ref-trudew_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trudew-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and was commonly known as <b>Idlewild Airport</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-trubls_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trubls-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination</a> in 1963, the airport was renamed John F. Kennedy International Airport as a tribute to the 35th President.<sup id="cite_ref-ageaus_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ageaus-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyatn_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyatn-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Terminal_6_(Sundrome)"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Terminal 6 (Sundrome)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Terminal_8_(1960)"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Terminal 8 (1960)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#Terminal_9"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Terminal 9</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Tower_Air_terminal"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Tower Air terminal</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Runways"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Runways</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Operational_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Operational facilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Other_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Other facilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Information_services"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Information services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Airport_hotels"><span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Airport hotels</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Ground_transportation"><span class="tocnumber">2.8</span> <span class="toctext">Ground transportation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Airlines_and_destinations"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Airlines and destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Passenger"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Passenger</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">3.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Cargo"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cargo</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Passenger_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Passenger numbers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Top_destinations"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Top destinations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Airline_market_share"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Airline market share</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Accidents_and_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Notable_staff"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notable staff</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#&quot;Kennedy_Steve&quot;"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">"Kennedy Steve"</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Notes_and_references"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notes and references</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png/220px-Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png/330px-Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png/440px-Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png 2x" data-file-width="2652" data-file-height="2582" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airports_New_York_City_Map_Julius_Schorzman.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing New York City and the locations of JFK (1), <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">LaGuardia</a> (2), and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a> (3) airports</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>John F. Kennedy International Airport was originally called <b>Idlewild Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>IDL</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>KIDL</b>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Location_identifier" title="Location identifier">LID</a>: <b>IDL</b>) after the Idlewild Beach Golf Course that it displaced. It was built to relieve <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">LaGuardia Field</a>, which had become overcrowded after its 1939 opening.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> In late 1941, mayor <a href="/wiki/Fiorello_La_Guardia" title="Fiorello La Guardia">Fiorello La Guardia</a> announced that the city had tentatively chosen a large area of marshland on <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Bay" title="Jamaica Bay">Jamaica Bay</a>, which included the Idlewild Golf Course as well as a summer hotel and a <a href="/wiki/Landing_strip" class="mw-redirect" title="Landing strip">landing strip</a> called the Jamaica Sea-Airport, for a new airfield.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Title_(property)" title="Title (property)">Title</a> to the land was conveyed to the city at the end of December 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Construction began in 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-mammth43_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mammth43-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> though the airport\'s final layout was not yet decided upon.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2\xe2\x80\x933</span></sup>\n</p><p>About US$60&#160;million was initially spent with governmental funding, but only 1,000 acres (400&#160;ha) of the Idlewild Golf Course site were earmarked for use.<sup id="cite_ref-newsday_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsday-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The project was renamed <b>Major General Alexander E. Anderson Airport</b> in 1943 after a Queens resident who had commanded a Federalized National Guard unit in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">southern United States</a> and died in late 1942. The renaming was vetoed by Mayor La Guardia and reinstated by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Council" title="New York City Council">New York City Council</a>; in common usage, the airport was still called "Idlewild".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1944, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Board_of_Estimate" title="New York City Board of Estimate">New York City Board of Estimate</a> authorized the condemnation of another 1,350 acres (550&#160;ha) for Idlewild.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Port of New York Authority (now the <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a>) leased the Idlewild property from the City of New York in 1947<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> and maintains this lease today.<sup id="cite_ref-panynj_pr_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panynj_pr-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In March 1948, the City Council changed the official name to <b>New York International Airport, Anderson Field</b>, but the common name remained "Idlewild" until December 24, 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-nyatn_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyatn-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The airport was intended as the world\'s largest and most efficient, with "no confusion and no congestion".<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_operations">Early operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first flight from Idlewild was on July 1, 1948, with the opening ceremony attended by then-U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newsday_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsday-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Port Authority canceled foreign airlines\' permits to use LaGuardia, forcing them to move to Idlewild during the next couple of years.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Idlewild at the time had a single 79,280-square-foot (7,365&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) terminal building;<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> by 1949, the terminal building was being expanded to 215,501 square feet (20,021&#160;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Further expansions would come in following years, including a control tower in 1952,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> as well as new and expanded buildings and <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Idlewild opened with six runways and a seventh under construction;<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> runways 1L and 7L were held in reserve and never came into use as runways. Runway 31R (originally 8,000&#160;ft or 2,438&#160;m) is still in use; runway 31L (originally 9,500&#160;ft or 2,896&#160;m) opened soon after the rest of the airport and is still in use; runway 1R closed in 1957 and runway 7R closed around 1966. Runway 4 (originally 8,000&#160;ft, now runway 4L) opened June 1949 and runway 4R was added ten years later. A smaller runway 14/32 was built after runway 7R closed and was used until 1990<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/STOL" title="STOL">STOL</a>, and smaller commuter flights.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Avro_Jetliner" class="mw-redirect" title="Avro Jetliner">Avro Jetliner</a> was the first jet airliner to land at Idlewild on April 16, 1950. A <a href="/wiki/Sud_Aviation_Caravelle" title="Sud Aviation Caravelle">Sud Aviation Caravelle</a> prototype was the next airliner to land at Idlewild, on May 2, 1957. Later in 1957, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a> sought approval for two <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-104" title="Tupolev Tu-104">Tupolev Tu-104</a> flights carrying diplomats to Idlewild; the Port Authority did not allow them, saying noise tests had to be done first. (The Caravelle had been tested at Paris.)\n</p><p>In 1951, the airport averaged 73 daily airline operations (takeoffs plus landings); the October 1951 <i>Airline Guide</i> shows nine domestic departures a day on National and Northwest. Much of Newark\'s traffic moved to Idlewild (which averaged 242 daily airline operations in 1952) when Newark closed in February 1952. L-1049 Constellations and DC-7s appeared between 1951 and 1953 and did not use LaGuardia for their first several years, bringing more traffic to Idlewild. The April 1957 <i>Airline Guide</i> cites a total of 1,283 departures a week, including about 250 from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a>, 150 from <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(1934%E2%80%931980)" title="National Airlines (1934\xe2\x80\x931980)">National Airlines</a> and 130 from <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (March 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Separate_terminals">Separate terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Separate terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By 1954, Idlewild had the highest volume of international air traffic of any airport globally.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The Port of New York Authority originally planned a single 55-gate terminal, but the major airlines did not agree with this plan, arguing that the terminal would be far too small for future traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-gordon_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Architect <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Harrison" title="Wallace Harrison">Wallace Harrison</a> then designed a plan for each major airline at the airport to be given its own space to develop its own terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-pearman_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pearman-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> This scheme made construction more practical, made terminals more navigable, and introduced incentives for airlines to compete with each other for the best design.<sup id="cite_ref-gordon_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The revised plan met airline approval in 1955, with seven terminals initially planned. Five terminals were for individual airlines, one was for three airlines, and one was for international arrivals. (National Airlines and British Airways arrived later.)<sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In addition, there would be an 11-story control tower, roadways, parking lots, taxiways, and a reflecting lagoon in the center.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> The airport was designed for aircraft up to 300,000-pound (140,000&#160;kg) gross weight<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The airport had to be modified in the late 1960s to accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>\'s weight.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The International Arrivals Building, or IAB, was the first new terminal at the airport, opening in December 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The building was designed by <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings,_and_Merrill" class="mw-redirect" title="Skidmore, Owings, and Merrill">Skidmore, Owings, and Merrill</a> (SOM).<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup> The terminal stretched nearly 2,300 feet (700 meters) and was parallel to runway 7R. The terminal had "finger" piers at right-angles to the main building allowing more aircraft to park, an innovation at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The building was expanded in 1970 to accommodate jetways. However, by the 1990s the overcrowded building was showing its age and it did not provide adequate space for security checkpoints. It was demolished in 2000 and replaced with Terminal 4.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a><sup id="cite_ref-DeltaT9_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeltaT9-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> opened Terminal 7 (later renumbered Terminal 9), a SOM design similar to the IAB,<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3\xe2\x80\x934</span></sup> in October 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> It was demolished in 2008.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Airlines">Eastern Airlines</a> opened their Chester L. Churchill-designed Terminal 1<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup> in November 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The terminal was demolished in 1995 and replaced with the current Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> opened Terminal 8 in February 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Kahn_and_Jacobs" class="mw-redirect" title="Kahn and Jacobs">Kahn and Jacobs</a><sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and had a 317-foot (97&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Stained_glass" title="Stained glass">stained-glass</a> facade designed by Robert Sowers,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> the largest stained-glass installation in the world until 1979. The facade was removed in 2007 as the terminal was demolished to make room for the new Terminal 8; American cited the prohibitive cost of removing the enormous installation.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a> opened the <a href="/wiki/Worldport_(Pan_Am)" title="Worldport (Pan Am)">Worldport</a> (later Terminal 3) in 1960, designed by Tippetts-Abbett-McCarthy-Stratton.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCL-1915_16-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCL-1915-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>4</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> It featured a large, elliptical roof suspended by 32 sets of radial posts and cables; the roof extended 114 feet (35&#160;m) beyond the base of the terminal to cover the passenger loading area. It was one of the first airline terminals in the world to feature <a href="/wiki/Jetway" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetway">Jetways</a> that connected to the terminal and that could be moved to provide an easy walkway for passengers from the terminal to a docked aircraft. Jetways replaced the need to have to board the plane outside via <a href="/wiki/Airstairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Airstairs">airstairs</a>, which descend from an aircraft, via truck-mounted mobile stairs or via wheeled stairs.<sup id="cite_ref-time_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The Worldport was demolished in 2013.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a> opened the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_Center" title="TWA Flight Center">TWA Flight Center</a> in 1962, designed by <a href="/wiki/Eero_Saarinen" title="Eero Saarinen">Eero Saarinen</a> with a distinctive winged-bird shape.<sup id="cite_ref-exam1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exam1-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bglobe_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bglobe-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> With the demise of TWA in 2001, the terminal remained vacant until 2005 when <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a> (PANYNJ) financed the construction of a new 26-gate terminal partly encircling the Saarinen building. Called Terminal 5 (Now T5), the new terminal opened October 22, 2008. T5 is connected to the Saarinen central building through the original passenger departure-arrival tubes that connected the building to the outlying gates. The original Saarinen terminal, also known as the head house, has since been converted into the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Hotel" title="TWA Hotel">TWA Hotel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braniff_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Braniff International">Braniff International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines" title="Northeast Airlines">Northeast Airlines</a> opened a joint terminal in November 1962 (now Terminal 2).<sup id="cite_ref-time_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(NA)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Airlines (NA)">National Airlines</a> opened the <a href="/wiki/Sundrome" title="Sundrome">Sundrome</a> (later Terminal 6) in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The terminal was designed by <a href="/wiki/Pei_Cobb_Freed_%26_Partners" title="Pei Cobb Freed &amp; Partners">I.M.Pei</a>. It was unique for its use of all-glass <a href="/wiki/Mullion" title="Mullion">mullions</a> dividing the window sections, unprecedented at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> planned to redevelop this terminal and the TWA Flight Center as a new United terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 6 was used by <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> from 2001 through 2008, and then was vacated and demolished when <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> moved to Terminal 5.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_operation">Later operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Later operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport was renamed John F. Kennedy International Airport on December 24, 1963, a month and two days after the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination</a> of <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Mayor <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Wagner,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Robert F. Wagner, Jr.">Robert F. Wagner, Jr.</a> proposed the renaming to JFK.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The IDL and KIDL codes have since been reassigned to <a href="/wiki/Indianola_Municipal_Airport" title="Indianola Municipal Airport">Indianola Municipal Airport</a> in Mississippi.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airlines began scheduling jets to Idlewild in 1958\xe2\x80\x9359; LaGuardia did not get jets until 1964, and JFK became New York\'s busiest airport. It had more airline takeoffs and landings than LaGuardia and Newark combined from 1962 to 1967 and was the second-busiest airport in the country, peaking at 403,981 airline operations in 1967. LaGuardia received a new terminal and longer runways from 1960 to 1966. By the mid- 1970s, the two airports had roughly-equal airline traffic (by flight count); Newark was in third place until the 1980s, except during LaGuardia\'s reconstruction. The <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>, operated by <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, made scheduled trans-Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Supersonic" class="mw-redirect" title="Supersonic">supersonic</a> flights to JFK from November 22, 1977, until its retirement by British Airways on October 24, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Air France had retired the aircraft in May 2003.\n</p><p>Construction of the <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_JFK" title="AirTrain JFK">AirTrain JFK</a> people-mover system began in 1998, after decades of planning for a direct rail link to the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-JFKExp-Jan2005_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-JFKExp-Jan2005-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Although the system was originally scheduled to open in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-tl20020418_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tl20020418-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> it opened on December 17, 2003 after delays caused by construction and a fatal crash.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20031214_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20031214-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The rail network links each airport terminal to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a> at <a href="/wiki/Howard_Beach,_Queens" title="Howard Beach, Queens">Howard Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica,_Queens" title="Jamaica, Queens">Jamaica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-airtrain_2006_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airtrain_2006-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport\'s new Terminal 1 opened on May 28, 1998; Terminal 4, the $1.4&#160;billion replacement for the International Arrivals Building, opened on May 24, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>\'s Terminal 5 incorporates the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_Center" title="TWA Flight Center">TWA Flight Center</a>, and Terminals 8 and 9 were demolished and rebuilt as Terminal 8 for the <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> hub. The Port Authority Board of Commissioners approved a $20&#160;million planning study for the redevelopment of Terminals 2 and 3, the <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> hub, in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-panynj.gov_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panynj.gov-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 19, 2007, JFK was the first airport in the United States to receive a passenger <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> flight. The route, with an over-500-passenger capacity, was operated by Lufthansa and Airbus and arrived at Terminal 1. On August 1, 2008, it received the first regularly-scheduled commercial A380 flight to the United States (on <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>\' New York\xe2\x80\x93Dubai route) at Terminal 4.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Although the service was suspended in 2009 due to poor demand,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> the aircraft was reintroduced in November 2010. Airlines operating A380s to JFK include <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore</a> route),<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris</a> route), <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a> route), <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Incheon_International_Airport" title="Incheon International Airport">Seoul</a> route), <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a> (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93Seoul route), <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> on its New York\xe2\x80\x93Abu Dhabi route, and Emirates (on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Milan_Malpensa_Airport" title="Milan Malpensa Airport">Milan</a>\xe2\x80\x93Dubai and New York\xe2\x80\x93Dubai routes).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On December 8, 2015, JFK was the first U.S. airport to receive a commercial <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350</a> flight when <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> began using the aircraft on its New York\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Hamad_International_Airport" title="Hamad International Airport">Doha</a> route.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 14, 2016, at 9:31&#160;pm, gunfire was reported at Terminal 8; shortly afterward, gunfire was also reported at Terminal 1. An investigation indicated that no shooting had occurred, but frightened travelers ran from the terminals onto nearby highways and runways.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_2016_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press_2016-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tracy_2016_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tracy_2016-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The terminals were temporarily shut down, and flights were rerouted.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_Melendez_2016_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_Melendez_2016-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Police, who were investigating, learned that the reported gunshots were travelers clapping for <a href="/wiki/Usain_Bolt" title="Usain Bolt">Usain Bolt</a> after he won the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_100_metres" title="Athletics at the 2016 Summer Olympics \xe2\x80\x93 Men&#39;s 100 metres">men\'s 100-meter</a> dash at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_2016_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press_2016-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Two people were injured in the resulting stampede, and the Port Authority Police Department later reviewed its strategy for dealing with possible terror attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-Tracy_2016_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tracy_2016-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reconstruction">Reconstruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Reconstruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On January 4, 2017, the office of New York governor <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> announced a plan to renovate most of the airport\'s existing infrastructure at a cost of $7 to $10&#160;billion. The Airport Master Plan Advisory Panel had reported that JFK, ranked 59th out of the world\'s top 100 airports by <a href="/wiki/Skytrax" title="Skytrax">Skytrax</a>, was expected to experience severe capacity constraints from increased use.<sup id="cite_ref-amny20170104_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amny20170104-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nym20170105_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nym20170105-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The airport was expected to serve about 75 million annual passengers in 2020 and 100&#160;million by 2050, up from 60&#160;million when the report was published.<sup id="cite_ref-amny20170104_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amny20170104-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The panel had several recommendations, including enlarging the newer terminals; relocating older terminals; reconfiguring highway ramps and increasing the number of lanes on the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_678" title="Interstate 678">Van Wyck Expressway</a>; lengthening AirTrain JFK trainsets or connecting the line to the New York City transportation system, and rebuilding the <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_(LIRR_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaica (LIRR station)">Jamaica station</a> with direct connections to the Long Island Rail Road and the New York City Subway.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> No start date has yet been proposed for the project;<sup id="cite_ref-nym20170105_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nym20170105-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> in July 2017, Cuomo\'s office began accepting proposals for master plans to renovate the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2018, Cuomo released details of a $13&#160;billion plan to rebuild passenger facilities and approaches to JFK Airport. Two all-new international terminals would be built, and the total number of gates would be brought up from 128 to 149. One of the terminals, a $7&#160;billion, 23-gate structure replacing terminals 1 and 2 (and the vacant space of Terminal 3) and connecting to Terminal 4, would be financed and built by a partnership between <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a> Group, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The other terminal, a new Terminal 6 costing $3&#160;billion, would be developed by  a consortium including JetBlue, RXR Realty, and <a href="/wiki/Vantage_Airport_Group" title="Vantage Airport Group">Vantage Airport Group</a> known as JFK Millennium Partners, and will replace Terminal 7 and the vacant space of Terminal 6, and would connect to Terminal 5. Terminal 8 would remain a separate terminal operating American Airlines and AA\'s partner Oneworld flights.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYGov-newjfk_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYGov-newjfk-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYDN-newjfk_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYDN-newjfk-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> JFK\'s redesign will include adding cars to AirTrain trainsets; widening connector ramps between the Van Wyck Expressway and Grand Central Parkway in Kew Gardens; and adding another lane in each direction to the Van Wyck, at a combined cost of $1.5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-Solution-JFK-2018-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> If approved, construction is expected to begin in 2020. Under the plan, the first gates would open in 2023, and the project would be complete in 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-NYGov-newjfk_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYGov-newjfk-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYDN-newjfk_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYDN-newjfk-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 7, 2020, construction began on expanding and improving Terminal 8. Following the construction, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a> will move into Terminal 8. This construction will be the first phase in the airport\'s expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-airport-technology.com_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-technology.com-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On February 11, 2020, Cuomo and the Port Authority, along with Delta Air Lines, announced a $3.8 billion plan to add sixteen domestic gates to the \'A\' side of Terminal 4. The main headhouse will be expanded to accommodate additional passengers and would open in 2022. The sixteen new gates will open in 2023, allowing the demolition of Terminal 2, the consolidation of flights for Delta, and the ability to build the new Terminal 1. An expanded roadway will be completed in 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>JFK has six terminals, containing 131 gates in total. The terminals are numbered 1\xe2\x80\x938 but skipping terminals 3 (demolished in 2013) and 6 (demolished in 2011).\n</p><p>The terminal buildings, with the exception of the former <a href="/wiki/Tower_Air" title="Tower Air">Tower Air</a> terminal, are arranged in a deformed U-shaped wavy pattern around a central area containing parking, a power plant and other airport facilities. The terminals are connected by the <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_JFK" title="AirTrain JFK">AirTrain</a> system and access roads. Directional signage throughout the terminals was designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mijksenaar" title="Paul Mijksenaar">Paul Mijksenaar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A 2006 survey by <a href="/wiki/J.D._Power_and_Associates" class="mw-redirect" title="J.D. Power and Associates">J.D. Power and Associates</a> in conjunction with <i><a href="/wiki/Aviation_Week_%26_Space_Technology" title="Aviation Week &amp; Space Technology">Aviation Week</a></i> found JFK ranked second in overall traveler satisfaction among large airports in the United States, behind <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">McCarran International Airport</a>, which serves the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas metropolitan area">Las Vegas metropolitan area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Until the early 1990s, each terminal was known by the primary airline that served it, except for Terminal 4, which was known as the International Arrivals Building. In the early 1990s, all of the terminals were given numbers except for the Tower Air terminal, which sat outside the Central Terminals area and was not numbered. Like in the other airports controlled by the Port Authority, terminals are sometimes managed and maintained by independent terminal operators. At JFK, all terminals are currently managed by airlines or consortiums of the airlines serving them, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a>-operated Terminal 4. All terminals except Terminal 2 can handle international arrivals that are not pre-cleared.\n</p><p>Most inter-terminal connections require passengers to exit security, then walk, use a shuttle bus, or use the AirTrain JFK to get to the other terminal, then re-clear security.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/JFK_Terminal_1.jpg/220px-JFK_Terminal_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/JFK_Terminal_1.jpg/330px-JFK_Terminal_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/JFK_Terminal_1.jpg/440px-JFK_Terminal_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Terminal 1</b> opened in 1998, 50 years after the opening of JFK, at the direction of the Terminal One Group, a consortium of four key operating carriers: <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> This partnership was founded after the four airlines reached agreement that the then-existing international carrier facilities were inadequate for their needs.\n</p><p>Terminal 1 is served by <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saudia" title="Saudia">Saudia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Maroc" title="Royal Air Maroc">Royal Air Maroc</a>. Other airlines serving terminal 1 include <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Airlines" title="Azerbaijan Airlines">Azerbaijan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Airways" title="Cayman Airways">Cayman Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Airlines" title="Philippine Airlines">Philippine Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/VivaAerobus" class="mw-redirect" title="VivaAerobus">VivaAerobus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 1 was designed by William Nicholas Bodouva + Associates.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodouva_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodouva-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It and <a href="#Terminal_4">Terminal 4</a> are the two terminals at JFK Airport with the capability of handling the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> aircraft, which are flown by Lufthansa on the route from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, and by Korean Air on the route from <a href="/wiki/Incheon_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Incheon Airport">Seoul\xe2\x80\x93Incheon</a>. Air France operated <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> here until 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 1 has 11 gates.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><b>Terminal 2</b> opened in 1962 as the home of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines" title="Northeast Airlines">Northeast Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braniff" class="mw-redirect" title="Braniff">Braniff</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a>, and is now exclusively used and operated by <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> for its hub at the airport along with Terminal 4. After the demise of Northeast Airlines and Braniff, the terminal was taken over by Pan American World Airways and subsequently by Delta. Since the opening of the Terminal 4 addition in May 2013, Terminal 2 has been designated as the C gates by Delta and has 11 Jetway-equipped gates (C60\xe2\x80\x93C70). Terminal 2 used to house the majority of Delta\'s operations, but after the opening of the Terminal 4 addition, the majority of flights are now handled out of the latter, including international and transcontinental flights.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 2 is currently temporarily closed.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_4">Terminal 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminal 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg/220px-JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg/330px-JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg/440px-JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFKNewYorkTerm4_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 4 replaced the former International Arrivals Building in May 2001.</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Terminal 4</b>, developed by LCOR, Inc., is managed by JFK International Air Terminal (IAT) LLC, a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Group" title="Schiphol Group">Schiphol Group</a> and was the first in the United States to be managed by a foreign airport operator. Terminal 4 functions as the hub for <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta</a> at JFK.\n</p><p>Airlines providing service at Terminal 4 include <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Aeromexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeromexico">Aeromexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, and <a href="/wiki/XiamenAir" title="XiamenAir">XiamenAir</a>; <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/EgyptAir" class="mw-redirect" title="EgyptAir">EgyptAir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a>; and non-alliance carriers <a href="/wiki/Air_Serbia" title="Air Serbia">Air Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Airlines" title="Caribbean Airlines">Caribbean Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Airlines,_LLC" title="Eastern Airlines, LLC">Eastern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">El Al</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> (late night international arrivals only), <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Airways" title="Kuwait Airways">Kuwait Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/LATAM_Brasil" title="LATAM Brasil">LATAM Brasil</a>, <a href="/wiki/LATAM_Chile" title="LATAM Chile">LATAM Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan_Airways" title="Uzbekistan Airways">Uzbekistan Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volaris" title="Volaris">Volaris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviation_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviation-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Opened in 2001 and designed by <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings_and_Merrill" class="mw-redirect" title="Skidmore, Owings and Merrill">Skidmore, Owings and Merrill</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> the 1.5-million-square-foot (140,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) terminal was built at a cost of $1.4 billion and replaced JFK\'s old International Arrivals Building or simply IAB, which opened in 1957. The terminal was expanded in the late 2000s and early 2010s. The first phase of Delta\'s $1.4 billion project at the airport which includes nine new international gates, additional baggage space, a centralized security checkpoint (moving two checkpoints into one location just after check-in), and customs and border-security facilities\xe2\x80\x94was completed on May 24, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Delta_opens_new_JFK_Terminal_4_hub,_Terminal_2_to_be_demolished_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delta_opens_new_JFK_Terminal_4_hub,_Terminal_2_to_be_demolished-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 4 has 38 gates in two concourses: A2\xe2\x80\x93A7, B18, and B22\xe2\x80\x93B55 with the exclusion of B40, B50 and B52. As of 2013, Delta and the Port Authority agreed<sup id="cite_ref-Minutes_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minutes-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> to an additional $175 million phase II expansion, which allowed Delta to construct 11 regional jet gates at Terminal 4, as well. The agreement allowed Delta to drop a previously planned physical connection that it wanted to build with the existing Terminal 2 and instead close T2. The work on the Delta hub was completed in January 2015, with funding primarily from $900 million in special-project <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Delta sought funding for the regional jet expansion from the New York City Industrial Development Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-Minutes_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minutes-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Terminal 4 was built during the construction of the AirTrain, the AirTrain station was built inside the terminal building. Other AirTrain stations are built across from terminal buildings. Delta has also moved much of its operations to T4, as it expands operations beyond T2, with T3 now closed. Concourse A serves as the stopping location for Asian and some European airlines, whereas Concourse B is made up of Delta flights, and a number of Asian and some European airlines.\n</p><p>Like Terminal 1, it is <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>-compatible, and <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a> (to Seoul),<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> (to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a>; both non-stop and one-stop flights via <a href="/wiki/Milan_Malpensa" class="mw-redirect" title="Milan Malpensa">Milan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> (to Abu Dhabi),<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> (to Singapore via Frankfurt) currently use Terminal 4 for their Airbus A380s. However, as of 2019 only one gate (A6) at Terminal 4 has three jetways, which is the generally preferred and most efficient system to board and offload an A380. A variety of other airlines from across the globe as well as SkyTeam and Star Alliance use the terminal as well.\n</p><p>According to Delta Air Lines, Concourse A will be expanded with 16 additional domestic gates, replacing Terminal 2.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_5">Terminal 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Terminal 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg/220px-JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg/330px-JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg/440px-JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_5_Ticketing_and_Check-In.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 5</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Terminal 5</b> opened in 2008 for <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>, the manager and primary tenant of the building, as the base of its large JFK hub. The terminal has also been used by <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Airlines" title="Hawaiian Airlines">Hawaiian Airlines</a> since June 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TAP_Air_Portugal" title="TAP Air Portugal">TAP Air Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a>, and Irish flag carrier <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, whose flights arriving into JFK from <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin airport">Dublin</a> have already been <a href="/wiki/United_States_border_preclearance" title="United States border preclearance">pre-cleared</a> in Ireland. Aer Lingus previously used Terminal 4 prior to the introduction of pre-clearance in Ireland, moving to Terminal 5 on April 3, 2013. On November 12, 2014, JetBlue opened the International Arrivals Concourse (T5i) at the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> TAP Air Portugal has used Terminal 5 since reinstating its JFK\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Portela_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Portela Airport">Lisbon</a> service on July 1, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The terminal was redesigned by <a href="/wiki/Gensler" title="Gensler">Gensler</a> and constructed by <a href="/wiki/Turner_Construction" title="Turner Construction">Turner Construction</a>, and sits behind the preserved <a href="/wiki/Eero_Saarinen" title="Eero Saarinen">Eero Saarinen</a>-designed terminal originally known as the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_Center" title="TWA Flight Center">TWA Flight Center</a>, which is now connected to the new structure and is considered part of Terminal 5.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The TWA Flight Center reopened as the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Hotel" title="TWA Hotel">TWA Hotel</a> in May 2019. The active Terminal 5 building has 29 gates: 1 through 12 and 14 through 30, with gates 25 through 30 handling international flights that are not pre-cleared (gates 28\xe2\x80\x9330 opened in November 2014).<sup id="cite_ref-T5i_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T5i-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The terminal has a TSA Pre check point for expedited security checks and is open from 3am to 11pm.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Airspace Lounge opened an airport lounge near Gate 24 in July 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and Aer Lingus opened an airport lounge in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In August 2016, <a href="/wiki/AirMall" title="AirMall">Fraport USA</a> was selected by JetBlue as the concessions developer to help attract and manage concessions tenants that align with JetBlue\'s vision for Terminal 5.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> During the summer of 2016, JetBlue renovated Terminal 5, completely overhauling the check-in lobby.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_7">Terminal 7</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_7.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JFK_Terminal_7.JPG/220px-JFK_Terminal_7.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JFK_Terminal_7.JPG/330px-JFK_Terminal_7.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JFK_Terminal_7.JPG/440px-JFK_Terminal_7.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Terminal_7.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 7 \xe2\x80\x93 Departure Level</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Terminal 7</b> was designed by <a href="/wiki/GMW_Architects" title="GMW Architects">GMW Architects</a><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> and built for <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">BOAC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a> in 1970. Currently operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, it is also the only airport terminal operated on US soil by a foreign carrier, although Terminal 1 is operated by a consortium of foreign carriers serving the building.\n</p><p>Airlines operating out of Terminal 7 include <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines" title="Alaska Airlines">Alaska Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> carriers <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>; <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> member <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas">Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas</a>; and non-alliance carriers <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines" title="Ukraine International Airlines">Ukraine International Airlines</a>.\n</p><p>Between 1989 and 1991, the terminal was renovated and expanded at a cost of $120&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The expansion was designed by William Nicholas Bodouva + Associates, Architects.<sup id="cite_ref-Bodouva_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bodouva-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, the Port Authority approved British Airways\' plans to renovate and expand the terminal. The $250&#160;million project<sup id="cite_ref-facts_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> was designed by Corgan Associates<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> and was completed in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The renovated terminal has 12 gates.<sup id="cite_ref-facts_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, British Airways extended its lease on the terminal through 2022, with an option of a further three years.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> BA also planned to spend $65&#160;million to renovate the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-runwaygirl_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runwaygirl-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Despite being operated by British Airways, a major A380 operator, Terminal 7 is not currently able to handle the aircraft type. As a result, British Airways cannot operate A380s on the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London-Heathrow</a> to New York flights, even though in 2014 there was an advertising campaign that British Airways was going to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-runwaygirl_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-runwaygirl-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> However, British Airways plans to join its Oneworld partners in Terminal 8,<sup id="cite_ref-bamove_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamove-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and it will not exercise its lease options on Terminal 7. When BA vacates the terminal, the Port Authority has chosen JFK Millennium Partners, a consortium including JetBlue, RXR Realty, and <a href="/wiki/Vantage_Airport_Group" title="Vantage Airport Group">Vantage Airport Group</a> to operate, and eventually demolish, the current terminal while it builds a new Terminal 6 to serve as a direct replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-newt6_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newt6-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2020 <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> announced they would be returning to JFK in February 2021 after a 5 year hiatus. As of Sunday, March 28, 2021, United operates transcontinental nonstop service from Terminal 7 to its west coast hubs in <a href="/wiki/SFO" class="mw-redirect" title="SFO">San Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/LAX" class="mw-redirect" title="LAX">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_8">Terminal 8</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terminal 8">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg/220px-A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg/330px-A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg/440px-A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A9roport_JFK_D%C3%A9cembre_2007_-_Terminal_9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inside the security checkpoint of Terminal 8</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Terminal 8</b> is a major <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> hub with <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American</a> operating its hub here.  In 1999, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> began an eight-year program to build the largest passenger terminal at JFK, designed by <a href="/wiki/AECOM" title="AECOM">DMJM Aviation</a> to replace both Terminal 8 and Terminal 9. The new terminal was built in four phases, which involved the construction of a new midfield concourse and demolition of old Terminals 8 and 9. It was opened in stages between 2005 and its official opening in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-term8_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-term8-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> American Airlines, the third-largest carrier at JFK, manages Terminal 8 and is the largest carrier at the terminal. Some Oneworld airlines that operate out of Terminal 8 include <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jordanian_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Jordanian Airlines">Royal Jordanian Airlines</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> carrier <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">Ethiopian Airlines</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> plans to move into Terminal 8 by the end of 2022 following its renovation and expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-bamove_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bamove-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 7, 2020, construction began on expanding and improving Terminal 8. The construction is estimated to be completed in 2022. British Airways will move into Terminal 8 following the construction and will provide 14 daily flights to London. This construction is the first phase in an overall plan to renovate JFK airport.<sup id="cite_ref-airport-technology.com_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-technology.com-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The terminal is twice the size of <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>. It offers dozens of retail and food outlets, 84 ticket counters, 44 self-service kiosks, 10 security checkpoint lanes, and a U.S. Customs and Border Protection facility that can process more than 1,600 people an hour. Terminal 8 has an annual capacity of 12.8M passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> It has two <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Admirals_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Admirals Club">Admirals Clubs</a> and a Flagship Lounge for premium class passengers.\n</p><p>Terminal 8 has 29 gates: 12 gates in Concourse B (1\xe2\x80\x938, 10, 12, 14 and 16) and 17 gates in Concourse C (31\xe2\x80\x9347).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Gate 31 is further subdivided into 5 regional service gates for small jets, 31A\xe2\x80\x9331E. Gate 32 is subdivided into 4 regional service gates for small <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jets</a>, 32F\xe2\x80\x9332I.
