The total number of <a href="/wiki/Jetbridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Jetbridge">jetbridges</a> is, therefore, 36. Passenger access to and from Concourse C is by a tunnel that includes moving walkways.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_terminals">Former terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Former terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>JFK Airport was originally built with ten terminals, compared to the six it has today. Ten terminals remained until the late 1990s, then nine remained until the early 2000s, followed by eight until 2011 and seven until 2013.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Air_Lines_terminal">Eastern Air Lines terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Eastern Air Lines terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>This terminal opened in 1959 and was demolished in 1995 after the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a> in 1991. The terminal was on the site of today\'s Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_3_.28Worldport.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3_(Worldport)">Terminal 3 (Worldport)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Terminal 3 (Worldport)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Worldport_(Pan_Am)" title="Worldport (Pan Am)">Worldport (Pan Am)</a></div>\n<p>Terminal 3 opened as the <a href="/wiki/Worldport_(Pan_Am)" title="Worldport (Pan Am)">Worldport</a> in 1960 for <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American</a>; it expanded after the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> in 1970. After Pan Am\'s demise in 1991 <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> took over ownership of the terminal and was its only occupant until its closure in 2013. It had a connector to Terminal 2, Delta\'s other terminal, used mainly for domestic flights. Terminal 3 had 16 Jetway equipped gates: 1\xe2\x80\x9310, 12, 14\xe2\x80\x9318 with two hardstand gates (Gate 11) and a helipad on Taxiway KK.\n</p><p>A $1.2 billion project was completed in 2013, under which Terminal 4 was expanded and with Delta subsequently moving its T3 operations to T4.\n</p><p>On May 23, 2013, the final departure from the terminal, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> Flight 268, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> <a href="/wiki/Ben_Gurion_Airport" title="Ben Gurion Airport">Ben Gurion Airport</a>, departed from Gate 6 at 11:25&#160;p.m. local time. The terminal ceased operations on May 24, 2013, 53 years to the day from when it opened on May 24, 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Demolition began soon thereafter and was completed by Summer 2014. The site where Terminal 3 used to stand is now used for aircraft parking by Delta Air Lines.\n</p><p>There has been large media outcry, particularly in other countries, over the demolition of the Worldport. Several online petitions requesting the restoration of the original \'flying saucer\' gained popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="International_Arrivals_Building_.28Original_Terminal_4.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Arrivals_Building_(Original_Terminal_4)">International Arrivals Building (Original Terminal 4)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: International Arrivals Building (Original Terminal 4)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The International Arrivals Building (IAB) was opened in 1957, and was replaced with current Terminal 4 in 2001.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_6_.28Sundrome.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_6_(Sundrome)">Terminal 6 (Sundrome)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Terminal 6 (Sundrome)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sundrome" title="Sundrome">Sundrome</a></div>\n<p>Terminal 6 had 14 gates.  It opened as the <a href="/wiki/Sundrome" title="Sundrome">Sundrome</a> in 1970 for <a href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(1934%E2%80%931980)" title="National Airlines (1934\xe2\x80\x931980)">National Airlines</a>.  National was the tenant of this terminal until it was fully acquired by <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a> in 1980.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a> then expanded into the terminal, referring to it as the "TWA Terminal Annex", later called "TWA Domestic Terminal".  It was eventually connected to the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_Center" title="TWA Flight Center">TWA Flight Center</a>. Later, after TWA reduced flights at JFK, Terminal 6 was used by <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/ATA_Airlines" title="ATA Airlines">ATA Airlines</a>, a reincarnated <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Airways_(1996%E2%80%931998)" title="Pan American Airways (1996\xe2\x80\x931998)">Pan American Airways (1996\xe2\x80\x931998)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnival_Air_Lines" title="Carnival Air Lines">Carnival Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_Airlines" title="Vanguard Airlines">Vanguard Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/America_West_Airlines" title="America West Airlines">America West Airlines</a>.\n</p><p>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a> began service from Terminal 6, later opening a temporary complex in 2006 that increased its capacity by adding seven gates.  Until 2008, JetBlue was the tenant of Terminal 6. It became vacant on October 22, 2008, when JetBlue moved to Terminal 5, and finally demolished in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The international arrivals annex of Terminal 5 now uses a portion of the site, and the rest of the site is used for aircraft parking by both JetBlue and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> (which operates from nearby Terminal 7), but will be occupied by the new Terminal 6, an annex to Terminal 5, planned to be fully opened by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-newt6_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newt6-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_8_.281960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_8_(1960)">Terminal 8 (1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Terminal 8 (1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The original Terminal 8 opened in 1960; its stained-glass fa\xc3\xa7ade was the largest in existence at the time. It was always used by <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and in later years it was used by other <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> airlines that did not use Terminal 7. This terminal was demolished in 2007\xe2\x80\x932008 and replaced with a new Terminal 8.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_9">Terminal 9</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Terminal 9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Terminal 9 opened in 1959 and was used by <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-lpc_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lpc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DeltaT9_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeltaT9-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Delta moved to Terminal 2 when they acquired <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines" title="Northeast Airlines">Northeast Airlines</a> in 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Braniff_International_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Braniff International Airlines">Braniff</a> moved from Terminal 2 to Terminal 9 in 1973, and operated in Terminal 9 until its bankruptcy in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-BraniffAnnual_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BraniffAnnual-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\nUnited used Terminal 9 from its opening in 1959 until it vacated the terminal in 1991 and became a tenant at <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>\' Terminal 7. Terminal 9 then became the home of American Airlines\' domestic operations and <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_(airline_brand)" title="American Eagle (airline brand)">American Eagle</a> flights for the remainder of its life. This terminal was demolished in the early-to-mid-2000s and replaced with a new Terminal 8.<sup id="cite_ref-term8_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-term8-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tower_Air_terminal">Tower Air terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tower Air terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tower_Air" title="Tower Air">Tower Air</a> terminal, unlike other terminals at JFK airport, sat outside the Central Terminals area in Building 213 in Cargo Area A. Originally used by <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan Am</a> until the expansion of the Worldport (later Terminal 3), it was later used by Tower Air and <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">TWA</a> shuttle until the airline was acquired by <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> in 2001. Building 213 has not been used since 2000. It is located next to the Delta Air Lines employees\' parking lot number 7, which was once the Tower Air terminal parking lot.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>John F. Kennedy International Airport spans 5,200 acres or 21 square kilometers (8.1&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-FAA_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> There are four runways (two pairs of parallel runways) surrounding the airport\'s central terminal area.<sup id="cite_ref-airnav_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airnav-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Length\n</th>\n<th>Width\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Instrument_Landing_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Instrument Landing System">ILS</a>\n</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>13R/31L</b>\n</td>\n<td>14,511 feet (4,423&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>200 feet (61&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>Cat. I (31L)\n</td>\n<td>Third-longest commercial runway in North America (the longest is a 16,000-foot (4,900&#160;m) runway at <a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a>, and the second longest is a 14,512-foot (4,423&#160;m) runway at <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">Las Vegas International Airport</a>). Adjacent to Terminals 1, 2, and 3. Handled approximately one half of the airport\'s scheduled departures. It was a backup runway for <a href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" class="mw-redirect" title="Space shuttle">space shuttle</a> missions.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> It was closed on March 1, 2010 for four months. The reconstruction of the runway widened it from 150 to 200 feet (46 to 61&#160;m) with a concrete base instead of asphalt. It reopened on June 29, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_New_York_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC_New_York-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>13L/31R</b>\n</td>\n<td>10,000 feet (3,048&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>200 feet (61&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>Cat. II (13L); Cat.&#160;I (31R)\n</td>\n<td>Adjacent to Terminals 5 and 7. Equipped at both ends with ILS and ALS systems. Runway 13L has two additional visual aids for landing aircraft, a Precision Approach Path Indicator (PAPI) and a Lead-In Lighting System (LDIN). The ILS on 13L, along with TDZ lighting, allows landings down to half a mile\'s visibility. Takeoffs can be made with visibility of one-eighth of a mile. It closed on April 1, 2019 for almost 8 months as part of a major runway modernization project that replaced the asphalt base with a concrete base and widens the runway from 150 to 200 feet (46 to 61&#160;m). It reopened on November 16, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>4R/22L</b>\n</td>\n<td>8,400 feet (2,560&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>200 feet (61&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>Cat. III (both directions)\n</td>\n<td>Equipped at both ends with <a href="/wiki/Approach_Lighting_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Approach Lighting System">Approach Lighting Systems</a> (ALS) with sequenced flashers, and touchdown zone (TDZ) lighting. The first <a href="/wiki/Engineered_Materials_Arresting_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Engineered Materials Arresting System">Engineered Materials Arresting System</a> (EMAS) in North America was installed at the northeast end of the runway in 1996. The bed consists of cellular cement material, which can safely decelerate and stop an aircraft that overruns the runway. The arrestor bed concept was originated and developed by the Port Authority and installed at JFK Airport as a joint research and development project with the FAA and industry.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>4L/22R</b>\n</td>\n<td>12,079 feet (3,682&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>200 feet (61&#160;m)\n</td>\n<td>Cat. I (both directions)\n</td>\n<td>Adjacent to Terminals 4 and 5. Both ends allow instrument landings down to three-quarters of a mile\'s visibility. Takeoffs can be conducted with one-eighth of a mile\'s visibility. It closed on June 1, 2015 for almost 4 months as part of a major runway modernization project that replaced the asphalt base with a concrete base and widened the runway from 150 to 200 feet (46 to 61&#160;m). It reopened on September 28, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_facilities">Operational facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Operational facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Departing_JFK.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departing_JFK.JPG/220px-Departing_JFK.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departing_JFK.JPG/330px-Departing_JFK.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Departing_JFK.JPG/440px-Departing_JFK.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2154" data-file-height="1432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Departing_JFK.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking at runway 4L/22R and out to sea.</div></div></div>\n<p>JFK has over 25 miles (40&#160;km) of taxiways to move aircraft in and around the airfield. The standard width of these taxiways is 75 feet (23&#160;m), with 25 feet (7.6&#160;m) heavy-duty shoulders and 25-foot (7.6&#160;m) erosion control pavements on each side. The taxiways have centerline lights and are generally of asphalt concrete composition 15 to 18 inches (380 to 460&#160;mm) thick. An illuminated sign system provides directional information for taxiing aircraft.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Air_Traffic_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Traffic Control">Air Traffic Control</a> Tower, designed by <a href="/wiki/Pei_Cobb_Freed_%26_Partners" title="Pei Cobb Freed &amp; Partners">Pei Cobb Freed &amp; Partners</a> and constructed on the ramp-side of Terminal 4, began full FAA operations in October 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-PEI_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEI-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> An Airport Surface Detection Equipment (ASDE) radar unit sits atop the tower. A gas-fired electric cogeneration plant generates electricity for the airport, with an output of about 90 megawatts (120,000&#160;hp). It uses thermal energy from the capture of waste heat to heat and cool all of the passenger terminals and other facilities in the central terminal area.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> At the time of its completion, the JFK tower, at 320 feet (98&#160;m), was the world\'s tallest control tower.<sup id="cite_ref-PEI_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEI-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> It was subsequently displaced from that position by towers at other airports in both the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and overseas, including those at <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield\xe2\x80\x93Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Hartsfield\xe2\x80\x93Jackson Atlanta International Airport</a>, currently the tallest tower at any U.S. airport, at 398 feet (121&#160;m) and at <a href="/wiki/KLIA2" class="mw-redirect" title="KLIA2">KLIA2</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia, currently the world\'s tallest control tower at 438 feet (134&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_airport_feb17.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JFK_airport_feb17.jpg/250px-JFK_airport_feb17.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JFK_airport_feb17.jpg/375px-JFK_airport_feb17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/JFK_airport_feb17.jpg/500px-JFK_airport_feb17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_airport_feb17.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>JFK airport- February 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>Aircraft service facilities include seven aircraft hangars, an engine overhaul building, a 32-million-US-gallon (120,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) aircraft fuel storage facility and a truck garage.\n</p><p>In the last few years, improvements have been made to terminals, roadways and inter-terminal transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/North_American_Airlines" title="North American Airlines">North American Airlines</a> had its headquarters in Building 141 along Federal Circle, on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> North American Airlines was one of the building\'s tenants; the building does have <a href="/wiki/Servisair" title="Servisair">Servisair</a> and VOA as tenants and Port Authority storage.<sup id="cite_ref-Table1_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table1-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Building 141 was originally a <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a> (PANYNJ) administration building.<sup id="cite_ref-JFKSchools_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKSchools-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In the 1990s it served as the PANYNJ police headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2000 an $800,000, 5,000-square-foot (460&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) annex of the building opened to serve students of <a href="/wiki/Aviation_High_School_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviation High School (New York)">Aviation High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_City" title="Long Island City">Long Island City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JFKSchools_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKSchools-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In 2003 Building 141 was dedicated in honor of Morris Sloane, a PANYNJ aviation employee.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hangar 17, originally occupied by Pan American and later Tower Air, found a new and important role housing artifacts from 9/11 that eventually made their way to the <a href="/wiki/National_September_11_Memorial_%26_Museum" title="National September 11 Memorial &amp; Museum">9/11 Museum</a> at Ground Zero.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Servisair" title="Servisair">Servisair</a> has its offices in Building 86.<sup id="cite_ref-Table1_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table1-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/CAL_Cargo_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="CAL Cargo Airlines">CAL Cargo Airlines</a> has its offices in Building 23.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Currently <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Cargo_Airlines" title="Nippon Cargo Airlines">Nippon Cargo Airlines</a> has its New York City branch in Cargo Building 66.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously <a href="/wiki/Overseas_National_Airways" title="Overseas National Airways">Overseas National Airways</a> (ONA) had its headquarters at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Tower_Air" title="Tower Air">Tower Air</a> existed, its head offices were in Building 178 and later in Hangar 17 at JFK Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> When Metro International Airways existed, its head office was in Building 178.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey_Police_Department" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey Police Department">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey Police Department</a> (PAPD) provides law enforcement, fire rescue and emergency medical services to the airport. Its JFK Command is based in Building 269.\n</p><p>PANYNJ operations and administrative offices are located in Building 14.\n</p><p>Three chapels, including <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Skies_Chapel_at_John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="Our Lady of the Skies Chapel at John F. Kennedy International Airport">Our Lady of the Skies Chapel</a>, provide for the religious needs of airline passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sheltair is the current <a href="/wiki/Fixed-base_operator" title="Fixed-base operator">FBO</a> on the field serving General Aviation traffic. The company became the first privately operated <a href="/wiki/Fixed-base_operator" title="Fixed-base operator">FBO</a> at JFK Airport in its 65-year history when it opened on May 21, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><br />In January 2017, the Ark at JFK Airport, a luxury terminal for pets, opened at a cost of $65&#160;million. Ark was built ostensibly so that people who were transporting pets and other animals would be able to provide luxurious accommodations for these animals. At the time, it was supposed to be the only such facility in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> However, in January 2018, Ark\'s owner sued the Port Authority for violating a clause that would have given Ark the exclusive rights to inspect all animals who arrive at JFK from other countries. In the lawsuit, the owner stated that Ark had incurred large operational losses because many animals were instead being transported to a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a> facility in <a href="/wiki/Newburgh,_New_York" title="Newburgh, New York">Newburgh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/VHF_omnidirectional_range" title="VHF omnidirectional range">VOR</a> station, identified as JFK, is located on the airport property, between runway 4R/22L and runway 4L/22R.<sup id="cite_ref-airnav_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airnav-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_services">Information services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Information services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the immediate vicinity of the airport, parking and other information can be obtained by tuning to a <a href="/wiki/Highway_advisory_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Highway advisory radio">highway advisory radio</a> station at 1630 <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> A second station at 1700 AM provides information on traffic concerns for drivers leaving the airport.\n</p><p>Kennedy Airport, along with the other Port Authority airports (<a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">LaGuardia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a>), uses a uniform style of signage throughout the airport properties. Yellow signs direct passengers to airline gates, ticketing and other flight services; green signs direct passengers to ground transportation services and black signs lead to restrooms, telephones and other passenger amenities. In addition, the Port Authority operates "Welcome Centers" and taxi dispatch booths in each airline terminal, where staff provide customers with information on taxis, limousines, other ground transportation and hotels.\n</p><p>New York City traffic reporter <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Wagenblast" title="Bernie Wagenblast">Bernie Wagenblast</a> provides the voice for the airport\'s radio stations and the messages heard on board <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_JFK" title="AirTrain JFK">AirTrain JFK</a> and in its stations.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_hotels">Airport hotels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Airport hotels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are several hotels adjacent to JFK Airport, including the Courtyard by Marriott and the Crowne Plaza. The former <a href="/wiki/Ramada_Plaza_JFK_Hotel" title="Ramada Plaza JFK Hotel">Ramada Plaza JFK Hotel</a> is Building 144,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> and it was the only on-site hotel at JFK Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-CHM_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHM-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> It was previously a part of <a href="/wiki/Forte_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Forte Hotels">Forte Hotels</a> and previously the <a href="/wiki/Travelodge" title="Travelodge">Travelodge</a> New York JFK.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Due to its role in housing friends and relatives of aircraft crash victims in the 1990s and 2000s, the hotel became known as the "Heartbreak Hotel".<sup id="cite_ref-AdamsonPhilly_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdamsonPhilly-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNNFamiliarTrag_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNFamiliarTrag-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In 2009 the PANYNJ stated in its preliminary 2010 budget that it was closing the hotel due to "declining aviation activity and a need for substantial renovation" and that it expected to save $1&#160;million per month.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The hotel closed on December 1, 2009. Almost 200 employees lost their jobs. As of 2009, the Port Authority hoped to build a new hotel on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-Fickenscher_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fickenscher-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 27, 2015, Governor <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> announced in a press conference that the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_Center" title="TWA Flight Center">TWA Flight Center</a> building would be used by the <a href="/wiki/TWA_Hotel" title="TWA Hotel">TWA Hotel</a>, a 505-room hotel with 40,000 square feet (3,700&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of conference, event, or meeting space. The new hotel is estimated to have cost $265&#160;million. The hotel has a 10,000-square-foot (930&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) observation deck with an infinity pool.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Groundbreaking for the hotel occurred on December 15, 2016, and it opened on May 15, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>JFK Airport is connected to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a> by <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_JFK" title="AirTrain JFK">AirTrain JFK</a>. It stops at all terminals, parking lots, hotel shuttle areas, <a href="/wiki/Car_rental" title="Car rental">car rental</a> lots, the <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_(LIRR_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaica (LIRR station)">Jamaica LIRR station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Beach%E2%80%93JFK_Airport_(IND_Rockaway_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard Beach\xe2\x80\x93JFK Airport (IND Rockaway Line)">Howard Beach-JFK Airport subway station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/IND_Rockaway_Line" title="IND Rockaway Line">IND Rockaway Line</a> (<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/A_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" title="A (New York City Subway service)">A</a></span>&#32;train) and <a href="/wiki/Sutphin_Boulevard%E2%80%93Archer_Avenue%E2%80%93JFK_Airport_(Archer_Avenue_Lines)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sutphin Boulevard\xe2\x80\x93Archer Avenue\xe2\x80\x93JFK Airport (Archer Avenue Lines)">Sutphin Boulevard\xe2\x80\x93Archer Avenue\xe2\x80\x93JFK Airport subway station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Archer_Avenue_Lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Archer Avenue Lines">Archer Avenue Line</a> (<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/E_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" title="E (New York City Subway service)">E</a></span>&#8203;,&#32;&#8203;<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/J_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" class="mw-redirect" title="J (New York City Subway service)">J</a></span>, and&#32;&#8203;<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Z_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Z (New York City Subway service)">Z</a></span>&#32;trains).<sup id="cite_ref-panynj-official_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-panynj-official-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several city bus lines link JFK to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Q3_(New_York_City_bus)" title="Q3 (New York City bus)">Q3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q6_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Q6 (New York City bus)">Q6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q7_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Q7 (New York City bus)">Q7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q10_(New_York_City_bus)" title="Q10 (New York City bus)">Q10</a>, <a href="/wiki/B15_(New_York_City_bus)" title="B15 (New York City bus)">B15</a>, with free transfers provided for subway connections. The B15, Q3 and Q10 buses all serve the Central Terminal Area via a dedicated bus stop at the former Terminal 6 (connection to other terminals via AirTrain JFK, with a direct walkway provided to Terminal 5), while the Q6 serves only eastern Cargo Area D and the USPS Airport Mail facility and the Q7 serves only Cargo Area C. There are also many private bus lines operating express buses to Manhattan, the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a> and Long Island.\n</p><p>New York City\'s yellow cabs, licensed by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Taxi_%26_Limousine_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="New York City Taxi &amp; Limousine Commission">New York City Taxi &amp; Limousine Commission</a>, offer a flat-rate service of $52 from JFK Airport to Manhattan, excluding tips and tolls. Since November 30, 2006, this flat-rate fare (excluding tips and tolls) applies to travel from Manhattan to JFK as well. Depending on the time of day, taxi travel from JFK to Midtown Manhattan can be as quick as 35 minutes or as long as 90 minutes. Door-to-door car service is another popular transportation option.\n</p><p>JFK Airport is located in southern Queens on the <a href="/wiki/Van_Wyck_Expressway" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Wyck Expressway">Van Wyck Expressway</a> (I-678), which can be accessed from the <a href="/wiki/Belt_Parkway" title="Belt Parkway">Belt Parkway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Parkway" title="Grand Central Parkway">Grand Central Parkway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queens_Boulevard" title="Queens Boulevard">Queens Boulevard</a>. A ring road connects the airport terminals to the Belt Parkway and the Van Wyck Expressway. The airport offers customers over 17,000 parking spaces, included in multi-level parking garages, surface spaces in the Central Terminal Area, a long-term parking lot and valet parking.<sup id="cite_ref-ken_facts_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ken_facts-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla, Inc.</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Tesla_supercharger" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla supercharger">Supercharger (fast vehicle charging station)</a> at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> There are also private off-site parking operators near the airport.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span>  Qantas flies the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">787 Dreamliner</a> from New York to Sydney as QF12 with a stop-over in Los Angeles, where passengers have the option to connect onto the airline\'s flights to <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Airport" title="Brisbane Airport">Brisbane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Airport" title="Melbourne Airport">Melbourne</a>. The airline does not have eighth freedom rights to solely transport passengers between New York and Los Angeles due to US government regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cargo">Cargo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cargo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When ranked by the value of shipments passing through it, JFK is the number three freight gateway in the United States (after the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Los_Angeles" title="Port of Los Angeles">Port of Los Angeles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port of New York and New Jersey">Port of New York and New Jersey</a>), and the number one international air freight gateway in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-USDT1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USDT1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Almost 21% of all U.S. international air freight by value and 9.6% by tonnage moved through JFK in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The JFK air cargo complex is a <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade_zones_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign trade zones of the United States">Foreign Trade Zone</a>, which legally lies outside the <a href="/wiki/Customs_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs area">customs area</a> of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> JFK is a major hub for air cargo between the United States and Europe. London, Brussels and Frankfurt are JFK\'s three top trade routes.<sup id="cite_ref-bts-cargo_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bts-cargo-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The European airports are mostly a link in a global supply chain, however. The top destination markets for cargo flying out of JFK in 2003 were Tokyo, Seoul and London. Similarly, the top origin markets for imports at JFK were Seoul, Hong Kong, Taipei and London.<sup id="cite_ref-bts-cargo_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bts-cargo-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>25 cargo airlines operate out of JFK,<sup id="cite_ref-bts-cargo_267-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bts-cargo-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> among them:\n<a href="/wiki/Air_China_Cargo" title="Air China Cargo">Air China Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABX_Air" title="ABX Air">ABX Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Air" title="Atlas Air">Atlas Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/CAL_Cargo_Air_Lines" title="CAL Cargo Air Lines">CAL Cargo Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cargolux" title="Cargolux">Cargolux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific_Cargo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathay Pacific Cargo">Cathay Pacific Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/EVA_Air" title="EVA Air">EVA Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_SkyCargo" title="Emirates SkyCargo">Emirates SkyCargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Cargo_Airlines" title="Nippon Cargo Airlines">Nippon Cargo Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express" title="FedEx Express">FedEx Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/DHL_Air_UK" title="DHL Air UK">DHL Air UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalitta_Air" title="Kalitta Air">Kalitta Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">UPS Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Air" title="Southern Air">Southern Air</a> and, formerly, <a href="/wiki/World_Airways" title="World Airways">World Airways</a>. Top 5 carriers together transported 33.1% of all revenue freight in 2005: <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> (10.9% of the total), <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express" title="FedEx Express">FedEx Express</a> (8.8%), <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a> (5.2%), <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Cargo" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean Air Cargo">Korean Air Cargo</a> (4.9%), <a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a> (3.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most cargo and maintenance facilities at JFK are located north and west of the main terminal area. <a href="/wiki/DHL_Aviation" title="DHL Aviation">DHL</a>, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express" title="FedEx Express">FedEx Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Cargo_Airlines" title="Nippon Cargo Airlines">Nippon Cargo Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> have cargo facilities at JFK.<sup id="cite_ref-bts-cargo_267-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bts-cargo-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> Cargo opened a new $102&#160;million cargo terminal at JFK with total floor area of 81,124 square feet (7,536.7&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) and capability of handling 200,000 tons annually. In 2007, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> opened a new priority parcel service facility at their Terminal 8, featuring 30-minute drop-offs and pick-ups for priority parcel shipments within the US.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" Air</a>\n</td>\n<td>1,138,000\n</td>\n<td>7.40%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>5\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines" title="Alaska Airlines">Alaska Airlines</a>\n</td>\n<td>808,000\n</td>\n<td>5.25%\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accidents_and_incidents_at_John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="List of accidents and incidents at John F. Kennedy International Airport">List of accidents and incidents at John F. Kennedy International Airport</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_staff">Notable staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id=".22Kennedy_Steve.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Kennedy_Steve&quot;">"Kennedy Steve"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: &quot;Kennedy Steve&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Stephen Abraham</b>, also known as <b>Kennedy Steve</b> (born August 16, 1962), is a former air traffic controller at John F. Kennedy International Airport;<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> where he worked from 1994 to 2017. He is known for his more "casual" ATC conversations with pilots while working as a ground controller; which resulted in him being known as "Kennedy Steve" on various channels on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>. In 2017 Abraham won the <a href="/wiki/Dale_Wright_Award" title="Dale Wright Award">Dale Wright Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Controllers_Association" title="National Air Traffic Controllers Association">National Air Traffic Controllers Association</a> for distinguished professionalism and exceptional career service to the NATCA and <a href="/wiki/National_Airspace_System" title="National Airspace System">National Air Space System.</a><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, he was hired as Airside Operations and Ramp Manager for Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_memorials_to_John_F._Kennedy" title="List of memorials to John F. Kennedy">List of memorials to John F. Kennedy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_O._Ward" title="Christopher O. Ward">Christopher O. Ward</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
